  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_633d5ea8-089c-4533-98c2-7861583b5f57'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer10487714439387266641">There's no police training stronger than a cop's instinct. Faith Mitchell's mother isn't answering her phone. Her front door is open.   <span id="freeText10487714439387266641" style="display:none">There's no police training stronger than a cop's instinct. Faith Mitchell's mother isn't answering her phone. Her front door is open. There's a bloodstain above the knob. Her infant daughter is hidden in a shed behind the house. All that the Georgia Bureau of Investigations taught Faith Mitchell goes out the window when she charges into her mother's house, gun drawn. She sees a man dead in the laundry room. She sees a hostage situation in the bedroom. What she doesn't see is her mother. . . . <br /><br /><br />""You know what we're here for. Hand it over, and we'll let her go."" <br /><br /><br />When the hostage situation turns deadly, Faith is left with too many questions, not enough answers. To find her mother, she'll need the help of her partner, Will Trent, and they'll both need the help of trauma doctor Sara Linton. But Faith isn't just a cop anymore--she's a witness. She's also a suspect. <br /><br /><br />The thin blue line hides police corruption, bribery, even murder. Faith will have to go up against the people she respects the most in order to find her mother and bring the truth to light--or bury it forever. <br /><br /><br />Karin Slaughter's most exhilarating novel yet is a thrilling journey through the heart and soul, where the personal and the criminal collide, and conflicted loyalties threaten to destroy reputations and ruin lives. It is the work of a master of the thriller at the top of her game, and a whirlwind of unrelenting suspense.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10487714439387266641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This is the 5th of a 7-part Will Trent series, but there are 6 books in the Grant County series that precede it. If you read the Will Trent series fir<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This is the 5th of a 7-part Will Trent series, but there are 6 books in the Grant County series that precede it. If you read the Will Trent series first, you will see spoilers that you won't want to know for reading the Grant County series. All the books in both series are fantastic, so I'd recommend you start with Grant County's "Blindsighted", the 1st in that series. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi Tara. Just read it and was good. But like you I have not read the earlier books in the series so was a little frustrated re being unaware of the ba<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi Tara. Just read it and was good. But like you I have not read the earlier books in the series so was a little frustrated re being unaware of the back stories of Will Trent and several of the other characters. Time over I would go back and start from book 1.. I saw another review which suggests it's even better to read the Grant County series first. Apparently some of Will's friends or whatever feature in those. Cheers. Brian. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_3462024806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3462024806" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3462024806?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3462024806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13337975729108236335"><b>Fallen is a fast-paced, action-packed, Faith Martin centered addition to the Will Trent Series.</b><br/><br/>When Faith Martin drives to her mother’s house to pick up her newborn daughter, Faith discovers her mother, Evelyn, is missing. Not only that, but there is also blood all over the house, a dead man in the laundry room, and bad guys ready to pounce on Faith. This all happens in the first chapter and the book never really slows down. Faith not only has to deal with being a new mother, but she also has to</span>
  <span id="freeText13337975729108236335" style="display:none"><b>Fallen is a fast-paced, action-packed, Faith Martin centered addition to the Will Trent Series.</b><br /><br />When Faith Martin drives to her mother’s house to pick up her newborn daughter, Faith discovers her mother, Evelyn, is missing. Not only that, but there is also blood all over the house, a dead man in the laundry room, and bad guys ready to pounce on Faith. This all happens in the first chapter and the book never really slows down. Faith not only has to deal with being a new mother, but she also has to deal with her mother’s kidnapping, her brother’s return (he’s an a**hole,), her baby daddy, and some dark secrets from the past. <br /><br />Will is there to support Faith both as a friend and partner. I love how these two play off of each other. Will is also dealing with Betty having an unfortunate encounter with a Hawk (this had me LMAO), the brief, yet annoying return of Angie, as well as his growing feelings for Sara. The "will they, won't they" question is finally answered.<br /><br /><b>After reading book 4, I really missed Faith, Amanda, and, of course, Betty. Fallen makes up for this by having the entire plot revolve around Faith, who after Betty, becoming even more of a favorite. I enjoyed seeing how her character has grown and also learning more about her family history.</b><br /><br />Onto book 6!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13337975729108236335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_178619059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178619059" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178619059?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Lee Child, Tess Gerritsen</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2011-favorites">2011-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2011-publication">2011-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=gory">gory</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178619059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6477555272016800236"><b>4.5 stars</b> I have a theory that it's nearly impossible to read a Karin Slaughter book in more than a day. She's one of the few authors whose books I NEED to get and devour on the day they're released because I'm so engrossed in the characters and have been waiting <i>a whole year</i> to find out what happens to them next. If you like your murder mysteries on the dark and gritty side, if you're fascinated by the seething violence lurking in the human psyche, this author is a definitely going to make your</span>
  <span id="freeText6477555272016800236" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b> I have a theory that it's nearly impossible to read a Karin Slaughter book in more than a day. She's one of the few authors whose books I NEED to get and devour on the day they're released because I'm so engrossed in the characters and have been waiting <i>a whole year</i> to find out what happens to them next. If you like your murder mysteries on the dark and gritty side, if you're fascinated by the seething violence lurking in the human psyche, this author is a definitely going to make your favorites list.<br /><br />This third installment in her Georgia series, which chronologically follows the Grant County and Will Trent series, absolutely delivers on the page-turning thrills. GBI agent Faith Mitchell comes home from work one day to find her mother missing, her baby locked in the shed, a dead guy in the living room, and a bloody handprint above the open door. What the hell is going on? And how can she investigate the situation when she's been implicated in the crime?<br /><br />Leading the investigation is Faith's partner Will Trent, who is still trying to hide his high-functioning dyslexia as well as his attraction to former coroner Dr. Sara Linton. Will is one of the most interesting characters I've ever come across--he is highly principled, a fantastic agent, and incredibly damaged by his childhood. Will's taciturn nature keeps most of his colleagues at a distance, but the painful patterns set in his past continue to shape the difficult circumstances of his present, and as usual he has to fight his demons so he can function in his job. Fans of this series have been waiting literally years for some measure of happiness for Will, and it's a pleasure to say that <i>Fallen</i> does not disappoint in that respect. <br /><br />Slaughter (that is, believe it or not, not a pen name) continues to deliver high-tension thrills, hard-nosed yet vulnerable characters and violent, fast-paced action. As with all her books, this latest installment is exceptionally well-written and meticulously detailed, as well as filled with fascinating insight into forensic pathology, police procedurals, and human behavior. If you've never picked up one of her books...what are you waiting for?<br /><br />********************************************************************<br /><br />For anyone who is interested in checking out this series, <b>please note that it's important to read them in order</b> since the author wrote two separate series that eventually merge. Here's the order in which they should be read:<br /><br /><b>Grant County Series:</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21718.Blindsighted__Grant_County___1_" title="Blindsighted (Grant County, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Blindsighted</a><br />Kisscut<br />A Faint, Cold Fear<br />Indelible<br />Faithless<br />Beyond Reach<br /><br /><b>Will Trent Series</b> <br />These two books can be read (in order) concurrently with the above, but read them before you read the third batch.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21717.Triptych__Will_Trent___1_" title="Triptych (Will Trent, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Triptych</a><br />Fractured<br /><br /><b>Georgia Series</b> (merging of two sets of characters)<br /><br />Undone<br />Broken<br />Fallen<br /><br />Fair warning that they are fairly violent and occasionally gruesome...so they are definitely not for the faint of heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6477555272016800236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_454449084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/454449084" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/454449084?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer454449084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16956327014566213731">Fallen by Karin Slaughter is a 2012 Dell/Random House publication. <br/><br/><br/>This fifth installment in the Will Trent series may be, arguably, I’m sure, the best one of the series thus far. <br/><br/>Evelyn is babysitting for Faith when she becomes a victim of a home invasion. Once Faith arrives, she finds Emma safe and sound, but Evelyn has been taken. <br/><br/>From this point on, the drama, action and suspense are a non-stop rollercoaster ride. Many burning questions are answered and some huge developments take place in t</span>
  <span id="freeText16956327014566213731" style="display:none">Fallen by Karin Slaughter is a 2012 Dell/Random House publication. <br /><br /><br />This fifth installment in the Will Trent series may be, arguably, I’m sure, the best one of the series thus far. <br /><br />Evelyn is babysitting for Faith when she becomes a victim of a home invasion. Once Faith arrives, she finds Emma safe and sound, but Evelyn has been taken. <br /><br />From this point on, the drama, action and suspense are a non-stop rollercoaster ride. Many burning questions are answered and some huge developments take place in the Sara/Will/Angie saga. <br /><br />Slaughter really knows how to create rich characters, both good and bad, and manages to blend personal dramas with crime stories with perfect precision and timing. <br /><br />I was pleased to see all the characters take part in this one, in one way or another, and I was so happy to finally learn the truth about Evelyn’s past, and see Will begin to heal and break away from some influences that have been holding him back. I just hope it sticks this time. <br /><br /><br /><br />I highly recommend this series, if you haven’t read it yet. Slaughter is one the best crime/thriller authors out there and Will Trent is a terrific character! I strongly suggest reading the series in order for the best enjoyment of them. <br /><br />4.5 stars<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16956327014566213731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1399348599" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399348599" />
    <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon"><img alt="♥Sharon♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417537732p2/12125670.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399348599?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Sharon♥" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon">♥Sharon♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399348599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8979485372408394418"><br/><b>
  <i>She didn’t flinch. She didn’t falter. Instead, she put her forehead to his, looked him in the eye and told him, “Breathe.” Will let out a breath he felt like he’d been holding his entire life.</i>
</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/Breathe_zpsf79lbqdc.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446085439i/16745940.jpg' alt=' photo Breathe_zpsf79lbqdc.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>I LOVE THIS SERIES. I LOVE WILL TRENT. ❤</b><br/><br/>From book to book there isn’t a connection with the plots. With each book you get a story that sucks you in right from the get go and doesn’t let you go until you turn that last page. Each of the characters are changing in ways that are intriguing. Karin Slaug</span>
  <span id="freeText8979485372408394418" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <i>She didn’t flinch. She didn’t falter. Instead, she put her forehead to his, looked him in the eye and told him, “Breathe.” Will let out a breath he felt like he’d been holding his entire life.</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/Breathe_zpsf79lbqdc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446085439i/16745940.jpg" alt=" photo Breathe_zpsf79lbqdc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>I LOVE THIS SERIES. I LOVE WILL TRENT. ❤</b><br><br>From book to book there isn’t a connection with the plots. With each book you get a story that sucks you in right from the get go and doesn’t let you go until you turn that last page. Each of the characters are changing in ways that are intriguing. Karin Slaughter is careful with what she reveals to the reader leaving you anxious to know more.<br><br>In <b>Fallen</b> the events that happen involve Will, his partner Faith, her mother Evelyn, a variety of other characters and of course Amanda. She sets my nerves on edge. I know I have said this before, but she makes me so nervous when she is around Will. She can be such a cold bitch. Her words are harsh and demeaning but there is something about her that rests just below the surface that makes you wonder. I wonder why she just doesn’t let Will go.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/c82b80112ed22357caec49dfe0c80b30_zpskkrpzghc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446085439i/16745941._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo c82b80112ed22357caec49dfe0c80b30_zpskkrpzghc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Faith has always been a tough cookie. She is stubborn, determined and has to be in control of her life at all times. When something happens involving her mother her world is shaken in such a way that she loses all her control. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/kristen-bell_zpsdjx41641.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446085439i/16745942.jpg" alt=" photo kristen-bell_zpsdjx41641.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And then there is <b>Will</b>. I love every damaged piece of this man. He isn’t your story book sexy as sin hero either. He is rather quirky and awkward. He is handsome and is body isn’t lacking by any means. But life has not been easy for Will. Not for one moment. He protects himself from happiness and always expects the inevitable. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/f8a8338f4937f74683457e0381189687_zpse1mndqol.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446085439i/16745943.jpg" alt=" photo f8a8338f4937f74683457e0381189687_zpse1mndqol.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sara is the wildcard in Will’s life. At least that is how I feel about her at the moment. I love her and I love what she represents to Will. Relationships with women have always been difficult for him. With Sara he feels things he hasn’t before. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/6ffd157b7d4261337c8284f45c2c3508_zpsaqshuhhf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446085439i/16745944.jpg" alt=" photo 6ffd157b7d4261337c8284f45c2c3508_zpsaqshuhhf.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As I said, in<b> Fallen</b> the characters are changing. The events that take place change Faith forever and things about Amanda and Evelyn’s past shed light on what they were like in their younger days on the police force. Their lives so intertwined. Will still battles his demons and Angie is still a BITCH. But something changes between them. It is about f’ing time.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/4e01d8cf70a8c50d2a13abe3ecb168cf_zpsvyw2nb5w.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446085439i/16745945._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 4e01d8cf70a8c50d2a13abe3ecb168cf_zpsvyw2nb5w.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8979485372408394418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8835440971585205419">5 Thrilling Stars<br/><br/><b>Oh My Goodness! Has My Heart Stopped Pounding?! I think Not!<br/><br/>Poor Faith Mitchell! My Heart was in my throat for most of this novel. </b> “Fallen” by Karin Slaughter got me good. I felt for Faith Mitchell so much I couldn’t imagine being in her position. Driving up to her mother, Evelyn Mitchell’s house, expecting to pick up her baby girl and finding blood on the door handle? Then discovering the house in disarray, her mother gone, a dead body and having to protect herself and her dau</span>
  <span id="freeText8835440971585205419" style="display:none">5 Thrilling Stars<br /><br /><b>Oh My Goodness! Has My Heart Stopped Pounding?! I think Not!<br /><br />Poor Faith Mitchell! My Heart was in my throat for most of this novel. </b> “Fallen” by Karin Slaughter got me good. I felt for Faith Mitchell so much I couldn’t imagine being in her position. Driving up to her mother, Evelyn Mitchell’s house, expecting to pick up her baby girl and finding blood on the door handle? Then discovering the house in disarray, her mother gone, a dead body and having to protect herself and her daughter against two assailants?!<br /><br /><b> All in the span of a few minutes?! Dear me! </b><br /><br />After what happened, Faith can’t even take part in the investigation! She has to leave it up to her boss Amanda Wagner and Will Trent. <br /><br /><u>It’s those Secrets that’ll Getcha! </u><br /><br /><b>What a Terrifying Thriller! I just Loved “Fallen!” Kudos to Karen Slaughter for giving the readers an action packed ride through CRAZY TOWN! </b><br /><br />I know I said I loved Faith Mitchell in my last review, but my love for her then didn’t compare to my love for her now! She is one strong woman! As for her partnership with Will Trent? I love how they have each other’s backs regardless. <br /><br />Thank you once again to my local library for the loan.<br /><br />Published on Goodreads on 2.17.20.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14616663738995525418">I don't know what it is about Will that endears me to him. He is not movie star handsome, he is socially inept in many ways, he is awkward. But he is lovable. He had a tough upbringing but that didn't make him mean and tough, quite the opposite actually.<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443122805i/16320623._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>He wasn't even her type.</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>We have a situation involving Lena, her mother, Amanda and a cast of characters from the past. But who is guilty? Who is innocent? Slaughter has a great way of writing where you seriously don't know who to believe. <br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
 </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14616663738995525418" style="display:none">I don't know what it is about Will that endears me to him. He is not movie star handsome, he is socially inept in many ways, he is awkward. But he is lovable. He had a tough upbringing but that didn't make him mean and tough, quite the opposite actually.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443122805i/16320623._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>He wasn't even her type.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>We have a situation involving Lena, her mother, Amanda and a cast of characters from the past. But who is guilty? Who is innocent? Slaughter has a great way of writing where you seriously don't know who to believe. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>She had been so stupid.<br>One mistake so many years ago.<br>One terrible, stupid mistake.</b>
</blockquote><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430251387i/14698150._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>

  <b>"It's slang for 'cunt'." She laughed.<br>"Why, Will, are you calling me a cunt?"<br><br>If only she knew how many times he'd been tempted.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Yeah, Amanda is a bit of a cunt alright.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443122805i/16320625.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>Will didn't look up. Instead, he took her hand. His fingers laced through hers.</b>
</blockquote><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443122805i/16320626.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Angie. What to say about her? I know she had a horrible upbringing but I cannot feel sympathy or empathy for her. I just cannot. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>This was their dance.<br>Anger.<br>Fear.<br>Violence.<br>Never compassion.<br>Never kindness.</b>
</blockquote><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443122805i/16320627._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I swear there was one scene and I was literally holding my breath.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>His breath caught when her hand slipped inside his shirt. Her fingers brushed over his chest, down his belly. She didn't flinch. Instead she put her forehead to his, looked him in the eye ...</b>
</blockquote><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443122805i/16320628._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Was there closure? Was there a HEA? Did they get their white picket fence in the country? You will just have to read it and see.... There is a lot more to come out in future books, I think. All I can say is that I love Will and Sara. And I hate Angie. Did I already say that?<br><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443122805i/16320629._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer569205466" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7014188540653294758">The story starts with a bang when GBI Agent Faith Mitchell returns to her mother, Evelyn's home to pick up her infant daughter, Emily, and finds a chilling situation. When the dust settles, the house is a major crime scene and Evelyn is missing. It's now a race against time to figure out the who, why and where. <br/><br/>I couldn't stop listening to this story, told from many characters' points of view. It was often difficult to keep up with all of the minor gangsters but it didn't matter...you knew they </span>
  <span id="freeText7014188540653294758" style="display:none">The story starts with a bang when GBI Agent Faith Mitchell returns to her mother, Evelyn's home to pick up her infant daughter, Emily, and finds a chilling situation. When the dust settles, the house is a major crime scene and Evelyn is missing. It's now a race against time to figure out the who, why and where. <br /><br />I couldn't stop listening to this story, told from many characters' points of view. It was often difficult to keep up with all of the minor gangsters but it didn't matter...you knew they were dangerous. One of the highlights was finally getting the truth of Evelyn's role in her former narcotics team's dirty activities. Another was Will and Sara's developing relationship, including his wife Angie. It was as complicated as I'd imagined. <br /><br />The writing, characterizations and storytelling are the finest. It's really hard resisting the need to jump right into the next book so I won't. This was just excellent. And, as usual, the narration, this time by Shannon Cochran, was pitch perfect.</span>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17716247-sandra-cross-my-heart?shelf=addictive-reads">addictive-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1163374029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14635981678633025075">I'm seriously running out of accolades for this series and author. Karin Slaughter is simply one of the best in Suspense & Romance Suspense. Once again, I found myself flipping/reading pages as fast as I could, heart pounding, anticipation soaring. <i>Fallen</i> starts off with a sense of impending doom as Faith is running late & fails to reach her mother, who is babysitting Faith's infant daughter, by phone. After finally reaching her home, Faith's fear ratchets up another notch at the sounds of her b</span>
  <span id="freeText14635981678633025075" style="display:none">I'm seriously running out of accolades for this series and author. Karin Slaughter is simply one of the best in Suspense &amp; Romance Suspense. Once again, I found myself flipping/reading pages as fast as I could, heart pounding, anticipation soaring. <i>Fallen</i> starts off with a sense of impending doom as Faith is running late &amp; fails to reach her mother, who is babysitting Faith's infant daughter, by phone. After finally reaching her home, Faith's fear ratchets up another notch at the sounds of her baby crying in a locked shed out back and at the bloody hand print on the backdoor of the house. The tension intensifies as Faith enters the house to find the kitchen splattered in blood, a dead man on the floor, and voices coming from upstairs. This all occurs in Chapter 1. Suffice it to say, the tone is set for the rest of the book. I really dislike spoilers so I won't say more. <i>Fallen</i> is intriguing &amp; tightly woven with twists &amp; turns - a mystery to be solved. And the character development is HUGE . . .Will, Sara, Faith, Amanda...secrets are revealed, bonds are formed. I have rejoiced &amp; cried with the characters of Grant County &amp; the Will Trent series. The developments in <i>Fallen</i> really touched my heart. Thank you, Karin Slaughter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14635981678633025075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

It just add that extras to make it so real that you almost believe you are reading a true story.<br><br>Although these books can be read as standalone stories I'm a sucker for the main characters and the relationships that develop between them, so I try and read them in order. Which made this book a favorite because Will finally stands up for himself, I love how he grows form book to book.<br>Actually I love how all the characters change and adapt.<br><br>I'm slowly running out of books for this series, which is kind of depressing. <br>I can't see my life without Will, Sara, Faith and Amanda in it.</span>

<div id="review_1691561936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1691561936" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1691561936?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1691561936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16390766514899019542">It is safe to say that I have "fallen" in love with Slaughter's Will Trent series. Slaughter has quickly become one of my favorite go to Authors. I love her writing, the suspense, the dialogue, the attention to detail, the character development and yes, even the blossoming love story. I really like how Slaughter gives us characters with flaws, with demons, with things that haunt them. For me it makes them more real, more believable and I just want to sometimes shake them silly, sometimes cheer f</span>
  <span id="freeText16390766514899019542" style="display:none">It is safe to say that I have "fallen" in love with Slaughter's Will Trent series. Slaughter has quickly become one of my favorite go to Authors. I love her writing, the suspense, the dialogue, the attention to detail, the character development and yes, even the blossoming love story. I really like how Slaughter gives us characters with flaws, with demons, with things that haunt them. For me it makes them more real, more believable and I just want to sometimes shake them silly, sometimes cheer for them, and sometimes want to give them a good hard smack on the ass to get them moving in the right direction.<br /><br />In this book, Faith (Will's partner) is running late to pick up her daughter at her Mother's home. When Faith arrives she quickly realizes something is not quite right and sees a bloody hand print on the door, her baby locked in a shed, a dead man, no sign of her Mother and shoots two men involved in the incident.<br /><br />Our hero, Will Trent is leading the investigation. Will continues to be reserved and a man of few words. He is still trying to hide his dyslexia which I wish he would just get over it's no big deal but to his character it is. He also continues with his beginning relationship with Sara (who we know from the Grant County series). Will perhaps Will always have demons that haunt him which is why he is probably so interesting and character with the most development. I predict we will learn more and more about him as he begins to open up to Sara. Speaking with Sara, like in the Grant County Series, she also helps with the investigation giving her expert medical opinions.<br /><br />This is a book where the past and the present collide for some characters. We learn some more about Evelyn, Faith's Mother. There are also some revelations made in Faith's own life.<br /><br />This was a very enjoyable fast read. I had to keep reading to see what would happen next. This is where Slaughter shines. She just knows how to write suspense/thrillers. My pages kept turning and turning. <br /><br />Looking forward to the next book in the series.<br /><br />See more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.openbookpost.com">www.openbookpost.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16390766514899019542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3083164798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3083164798" />
    <a title="Amanda Hupe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11658047-amanda-hupe"><img alt="Amanda Hupe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535036536p2/11658047.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3083164798?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Hupe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Hupe" href="/user/show/11658047-amanda-hupe">Amanda Hupe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11658047-amanda-hupe?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3083164798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3936806523451939194">It is official. I am halfway through the Will Trent series. I should be all caught up for when book 10 is released this year. Fallen by Karin Slaughter has to be the most suspenseful book in the series yet. In true Karin Slaughter fashion, the book begins with Faith Mitchell heading home from training and her mother, who is watching her daughter, isn’t answering the phone. She gets home and discovers a bloody handprint on the door and her mother gone. Her daughter is safely tucked away in the sh</span>
  <span id="freeText3936806523451939194" style="display:none">It is official. I am halfway through the Will Trent series. I should be all caught up for when book 10 is released this year. Fallen by Karin Slaughter has to be the most suspenseful book in the series yet. In true Karin Slaughter fashion, the book begins with Faith Mitchell heading home from training and her mother, who is watching her daughter, isn’t answering the phone. She gets home and discovers a bloody handprint on the door and her mother gone. Her daughter is safely tucked away in the shed. Faith has now gone from GBI Investigator to the victim, and also a suspect. Only Will Trent, Sara Linton, and Amanda Wagner can help. However, can Faith put her trust in them to bring her mother home?<br /><br />YES. YES. YES. I have a confession. I LIVE for Amanda Wagner. Sure, she has her faults but she doesn’t give a shit what anyone thinks and will take down anyone in her way. She is my hero and I want to be her when I grow up. After a serious lack of her character in the previous book, it was so refreshing to see her more often in this book. She takes on a bigger role since she is best friends with Evelyn Mitchell, who is Faith Mitchell’s mother. I swear Karin Slaughter if you kill her off in future books, I will crawl into a hole and cry for weeks. But you have my full permission to kill of Angie, Will Trent’s good-for-nothing ex-wife.<br /><br />As always, the cast of characters is fantastic and has a great dynamic. I love seeing them all have to team up and work together. They are like the dream team. Will Trent has a lot to deal with in this book. Faith is his partner and he refuses to lose her. But then there is the growing chemistry with Sara and the Angie problem. The growth over the last few books is fantastic.<br /><br />This book is just a huge avalanche of suspense. There is not a moment to breathe, so it causes problems when it is time to put the book down. Again, the ending is shocking and not even remotely predictable. I love it. I already borrowed, Snatched, from the library, which is book 5.5 in the series. Obviously, I rate this book 5 out of 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3936806523451939194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1426210499" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1426210499" />
    <a title="Piper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10095424-piper"><img alt="Piper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571200889p2/10095424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1426210499?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Piper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Piper" href="/user/show/10095424-piper">Piper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10095424-piper?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426210499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5403552477205292345"><b>Fallen</b>, the 5th in the Will Trent series, is hands down my favorite so far. I would give it more than five stars if I could. <br/> <br/>This was a very personal story for some of the regular characters we have come to know, which in turn made it personal for me as well (I’m very much invested in these people at this point). This wasn’t just a crime to <b>be</b> solved. It was a crime that <b>must</b> be solved- and with no less than a positive outcome.<br/> <br/>Faith Mitchell’s mother, Evelyn, is in serious trouble and Faith is</span>
  <span id="freeText5403552477205292345" style="display:none"><b>Fallen</b>, the 5th in the Will Trent series, is hands down my favorite so far. I would give it more than five stars if I could. <br> <br>This was a very personal story for some of the regular characters we have come to know, which in turn made it personal for me as well (I’m very much invested in these people at this point). This wasn’t just a crime to <b>be</b> solved. It was a crime that <b>must</b> be solved- and with no less than a positive outcome.<br> <br>Faith Mitchell’s mother, Evelyn, is in serious trouble and Faith is unfaltering in her quest to save her. She already has a lot going on in her life, but to lose her mother would be devastating- especially under these circumstances. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448940010i/17210754._SY540_.jpg" width="400”" height="604”&lt;br" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Amanda Wagner shows a different side of herself in this book. Evelyn is an old and very close friend of hers- and the emotions Amanda reveals while working to solve this crime are evidence of that. I was surprised to see that she might actually have a heart- which has been questionable up to this point! She also sees quite a bit of action which was rather interesting as well as humorous. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448940010i/17210755._SY540_.jpg" width="400”" height="553”&lt;br" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sara once again finds herself drawn into Will’s world, and becomes involved in the investigation. She’s not sure she wants to be there, but she has a soft spot when it comes to Will. There is finally a bit of advancement in their relationship, thankfully. Although, had it not been for her......<br><br><b>She had been so desperate for Will to fight for her that it had never occurred to her that Will was waiting for Sara to fight for him.</b> <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448940010i/17210756._SX540_.jpg" width="400”" height="267”&lt;br" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And then there is Will.</b> Beautiful, beat-down, selfless, quirky, loyal Will. He faced a myriad of emotions while working this case not to mention the physical danger he was up against. Between Amanda’s split personality, Faith’s fragile condition, Angie’s cruel and usual bitchiness (that’s the only mention she will get from me, and she doesn’t even deserve that), and the increasingly undeniable chemistry between Sara and him- he found himself frustrated and overwhelmed at times. I just want to wrap my arms around him and tell him that everything will be alright. He has no idea how many women love him (in the reading world anyway!!) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448940010i/17210757._SY540_.jpg" width="400”" height="509”&lt;br" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lastly, we are introduced to a new character, Roz Levy who is Evelyn’s neighbor. She was very interesting- to say the least. I wonder if she will grace us with her ball-busting presence in future books. And we again have the pleasure of seeing Charlie in action even if to a lesser degree than previous books. I like Charlie’s enthusiasm albeit a bit on the weird, geeky in a coroner’s sort of way. <br><br>I again would highly recommend Karin Slaughter's writing to the crime/drama enthusiast. This had plenty of gruesome, eewww moments as well as twists and turns that kept me guessing (although I did actually figure one part out early on). I loved it!! But even more- I love Will. ♥♥♥♥<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5403552477205292345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11044630592385540024">Can this author tell a story? I can easily say you're damn skippy she can. There was more content and dialogue packed in #5 than the others I've read in this series. Same cast of characters though....there are of course damaged Will (lysdexic but brilliant detective), bitch from hell Amanda (Will's boss), tough as nails Faith (Will's partner), the sweet doctor Sarah (Will's friend with benefits), and last but least the queen of skank Angie (Will's wife, but use this word loosely).   <span id="freeText11044630592385540024" style="display:none">Can this author tell a story? I can easily say you're damn skippy she can. There was more content and dialogue packed in #5 than the others I've read in this series. Same cast of characters though....there are of course damaged Will (lysdexic but brilliant detective), bitch from hell Amanda (Will's boss), tough as nails Faith (Will's partner), the sweet doctor Sarah (Will's friend with benefits), and last but least the queen of skank Angie (Will's wife, but use this word loosely). I'm telling you and as usual with Ms. Slaughter's novels I didn't see last few chapters coming or going.<br />I really like the fact that this series is set in Atlanta as I am a huge Braves fan and have spent many summer weekends and holidays at Fulton Cty &amp; Turner Field stadiums. I guess I didn't venture into the seedier areas of the city, guess that's why I'm able to live and breathe and attempt to review her books. Enjoy this series at your own risk, it usually takes me a day or two to fully absorb each one in this series. Especially tough listening at work....but please, don't tell anyone. &lt;)</span>

<div id="review_1400208276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1400208276" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6972914-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529600203p2/6972914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1400208276?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/6972914-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11055264-fallen">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1400208276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12572022798080947415"><b>5 STARS</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448981687i/17217086._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>WHOA! This series is really heating up now! And each and every character is being pushed to the breaking point. Whether it be in a good way or a bad. And as I get to know them, I am loving them all even more... or as in Angie's case, hating. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448981687i/17217087.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Will</b> is finally getting some happy in his life. Yes, it is completely immersed in turmoil, but it is there nonetheless. And while I think he has a long way to go cutting the cord with <b>Angie</b>, I am holding out hope that he can finally walk away from her</span>
  <span id="freeText12572022798080947415" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448981687i/17217086._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WHOA! This series is really heating up now! And each and every character is being pushed to the breaking point. Whether it be in a good way or a bad. And as I get to know them, I am loving them all even more... or as in Angie's case, hating. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448981687i/17217087.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Will</b> is finally getting some happy in his life. Yes, it is completely immersed in turmoil, but it is there nonetheless. And while I think he has a long way to go cutting the cord with <b>Angie</b>, I am holding out hope that he can finally walk away from her for good. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448981687i/17217088._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Sara</b> is also learning the ropes of how to get what she wants while negotiating the many obstacles that come along with Will Trent. She is quickly finding that she is going to have to change the rules of the game in order to have a part in his life. And even more surprising is her willingness to do whatever it takes.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Sara felt her mouth open in surprise. She was just as guilty as the rest of them. She had been so desperate for Will to fight for her that it had never occurred to her that Will was waiting for Sara to fight for him.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448981687i/17217089._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Angie</b> is definitely starting to lose her shit now. She has gone so far off the deep end, and has gotten so vicious towards Will that I find myself wishing something horrific will happen to her. I know that's terrible to say, but sadly true. She is just EVIL! Hate is too kind a word for what I feel for this bitch. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448981687i/17217090.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"They said the razor cut so deep that he scraped the bone." She smiled, as if this was a happy memory.<br>"He did that for me, bitch. You think he'd do that for you?"</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448981867i/17217104._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Faith</b> is front and center in this episode, along with her family. And while she's still struggling to get her health issues in order, she is as BADASS as ever! I really love her character. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Faith pumped the shotgun with one hand as she walked toward the carport. The action made a satisfying tha-thunk that echoed against the concrete. In a single fluid motion, the stock was against her shoulder, the barrel straight in front of her. She kicked open the door, holding the weapon steady as she yelled "POLICE!""</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448981687i/17217091._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We even got to see some rare moments of weakness on <b>Amanda</b>'s part. There is still a veil of mystery around her character, but we are definitely getting more and more clues about who she really is underneath all of that bravado. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"What did Evelyn tell you?"<br>"The truth, I hope."<br>"I'm sure it was buried in there somewhere."<br>"I think she told me what I need to know."<br>"She said you were proud of me."<br>"Well, that doesn't sound like me at all."<br>"No."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>This was by far my favorite book of the series so far. So, on to book 6! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12572022798080947415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2376079152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8057085907742748596">FALLEN is the best of the <i>Will Trent</i> series so far. And it has nothing to do with the murder/mystery of the week, though I'll admit I liked how it all shook out and how involved Amanda was. Seeing her character be more than the hardass chick with the brutal barbs was fascinating. And her backstory was something else, too. <br/><br/><b>But more importantly</b>. FALLEN is the best of the <i>Will Trent</i> series because of things that happened and all the things I felt in my feeeeeeelings place. Oh man. So much of this w</span>
  <span id="freeText8057085907742748596" style="display:none">FALLEN is the best of the <i>Will Trent</i> series so far. And it has nothing to do with the murder/mystery of the week, though I'll admit I liked how it all shook out and how involved Amanda was. Seeing her character be more than the hardass chick with the brutal barbs was fascinating. And her backstory was something else, too. <br /><br /><b>But more importantly</b>. FALLEN is the best of the <i>Will Trent</i> series because of things that happened and all the things I felt in my feeeeeeelings place. Oh man. So much of this was hard earned. So much of it isn't over. So much of it was beautiful while simultaneously ripping my heart out. I can't help but award it all the stars because of that. Even if so much of it made me want to burn down the world, too.. right after setting one particular person on fire. <br /><br />Even if the rest of the books end up being a disappointment (I don't think they will but I'm trying to prove a point here!), this book makes it all worth it. <br /><br />Thank you to my Slaughterthon ladies for holding my hand through this one and putting up with countless screenshots and voice memos. I'm sure there's a lot more still to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8057085907742748596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16470049646307423275">Another book passed on by my Mother In law, and frankly I must have upset her recently in some way. This was amazingly disappointing for a Karin Slaughter book.<br/><br/>Previous books of hers have torn along at a frantic pace, real page turners, but this felt like a plodding old horse, crying out to be put out of it's misery.<br/><br/>Normally the plots are rivetting and unfold in unexpected ways.   <span id="freeText16470049646307423275" style="display:none">Another book passed on by my Mother In law, and frankly I must have upset her recently in some way. This was amazingly disappointing for a Karin Slaughter book.<br /><br />Previous books of hers have torn along at a frantic pace, real page turners, but this felt like a plodding old horse, crying out to be put out of it's misery.<br /><br />Normally the plots are rivetting and unfold in unexpected ways. This felt like a non-story from start to finish. It was clear that the missing mother was alive, and was likely to remain that way, so no tension created. The story limps along from one murder to the next, with none of the characters dying having any emotional tie in to the reader.<br /><br />I'm used to having one unlikeable character in a Slaughter book (Lena Adams springs to mind easily in this regard) but this offering had them by the bus load. This made it even harder to buy into a poorly plotted book.<br /><br />There are some great Karin Slaughter books out there, but this isn't one of them. I'm hoping this is a deviation from the normally sparkling offerings. </span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780345528223" href="/book/show/10402306-fallen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=brain-candy">brain-candy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=police-procedural">police-procedural</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180337949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6036292297253587049">Karin Slaughter is my favorite go-to author for brain-candy police procedural reading. Her plots are fast-paced and interesting and her characters are so well-written. You may not like all of them and they may frustrate the hell out of you, but you are not bored by them. I have been waiting forever for this book to become available. I read it pretty much in 24 hours. It was so good. The plot is very good and kept me reading till 1 am this morning (despite the fact that I had to be up at 6am for </span>
  <span id="freeText6036292297253587049" style="display:none">Karin Slaughter is my favorite go-to author for brain-candy police procedural reading. Her plots are fast-paced and interesting and her characters are so well-written. You may not like all of them and they may frustrate the hell out of you, but you are not bored by them. I have been waiting forever for this book to become available. I read it pretty much in 24 hours. It was so good. The plot is very good and kept me reading till 1 am this morning (despite the fact that I had to be up at 6am for work). It's a pretty good plot because I thought it was about one thing, but in fact it's about something else entirely and I didn't really suspect the twist until I got within 20 pages or so of the end. Her sub-plot of Will Trent and Sara Linton is what I enjoyed the most. I really like Will Trent. He is the most intriguing, complex, and frustrating character I've been interoduced to in a long time (aside from the Dragon Tattoo's Lisbeth Salander). I'm rooting for him to succeed and break free of that bitchy wife of his (she is TERRIBLE) and the destructive relationship they have. I like how the beginning romance between Sara and Will was written--so subtle, but important and moving. This is a great book; a very satisfying read. I'm definitely looking forward to her next novel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6036292297253587049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1377254200" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1377254200" />
    <a title="Stephen Clynes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2982901-stephen-clynes"><img alt="Stephen Clynes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468231638p2/2982901.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1377254200?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen Clynes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen Clynes" href="/user/show/2982901-stephen-clynes">Stephen Clynes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1377254200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15571656546283980307">Faith Mitchell gets to her mother’s house late to pick up her daughter Emma but there is blood on the door. So starts this novel in the Georgia series of crime thrillers from Karin Slaughter. It has been over 5 years since I have last read one of Karin’s novels and it feels like I have suddenly bumped into an old friend I had lost contact with. I have read a total of 5 novels from Karin and each one is a stand alone book, so you do not have to read them in a sequence. Karin is a very popular top</span>
  <span id="freeText15571656546283980307" style="display:none">Faith Mitchell gets to her mother’s house late to pick up her daughter Emma but there is blood on the door. So starts this novel in the Georgia series of crime thrillers from Karin Slaughter. It has been over 5 years since I have last read one of Karin’s novels and it feels like I have suddenly bumped into an old friend I had lost contact with. I have read a total of 5 novels from Karin and each one is a stand alone book, so you do not have to read them in a sequence. Karin is a very popular top selling American author and she bangs out a new novel each year. I like her writing style where she bombards the reader with tonnes of information that supports an intelligent and very involved plot. She is very good with forensics and Police procedure.<br /><br />Karin is good at explaining popular culture in her novels so that the reader can step into the environment, for example…<br /><br />‘He’s only got one tattoo.’ Young gang members generally used their bodies as a canvas to illustrate their lives, etching tattoos of teardrops under their eyes for every murder, wrapping their elbows and shoulders in cobwebs to show they’d done time. The tattoos were always rendered in blue ink culled from ballpoint pens, what was called ‘joint ink,’ and they always told a story. Unless their story was so bad that it didn’t need to be told.<br /><br />...Karin also has a powerful knack to describe feelings to the reader so very well. We all enjoy everyday freedoms and can take them for granted, however…<br /><br />If they were lucky, this diagnosing and classification process took around six weeks before they were assigned to another prison or moved to the permanent facilities at D&amp;C. Until then, the inmates were on twenty-three-hour lockdown, which meant that but for one hour a day, they were confined to their cells. No cigarettes, coffee, or soda were allowed. They could buy only one newspaper a week. No books were allowed, not even the Bible. There were no TVs. No radios. No phones. There was a yard, but inmates were allowed out only three days a week, and that was weather permitting and only for whatever time was left on their one hour day. Only long-term residents were allowed visitors, and then it was in a room that was halved by a metal mesh that required you to yell to be heard over the voices of the other visitors. No touching. No hugging. No contact whatsoever.<br /><br />...I enjoyed reading Fallen, it was a very entertaining and thrilling read. It is a great story to run with as a daily read. It is easy to follow and picking it up is like getting the day’s gossip from workmates. Karin is in the top league of authors for crime thrillers and this book is a comfortable read that does not disappoint. I can find nothing wrong with this novel, so I will vote it the top score of 5 stars and look forward to reading her next novel called criminal in the Georgia series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15571656546283980307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3521424786" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7514594829999963566">A solid 3.5. Fast paced, easy to read but a bit repetitive in placed. Its been years since I read s Karin Slaughter book and I enjoyed following the adventure of familiar characters. Will Trent and his faithful chihuahua Betty. His domineering boss Amanda. His partner Faith Mitchell which the story centers around along with her mother Evelyn. Angie the wife of Will plays only a minor role in the story. <br/><br/>Faith comes open to a shootout at her mothers house. She kills two of the perpetrators in a ba</span>
  <span id="freeText7514594829999963566" style="display:none">A solid 3.5. Fast paced, easy to read but a bit repetitive in placed. Its been years since I read s Karin Slaughter book and I enjoyed following the adventure of familiar characters. Will Trent and his faithful chihuahua Betty. His domineering boss Amanda. His partner Faith Mitchell which the story centers around along with her mother Evelyn. Angie the wife of Will plays only a minor role in the story. <br /><br />Faith comes open to a shootout at her mothers house. She kills two of the perpetrators in a battle and finds her mother has been kidnapped while babysitting her daughter’s baby Emma who is safe. <br /><br />We then go on a roller coaster ride where diabetic Faith must save her mother. Sara Linton is also involved and finally gets together with Will. Lots of action, bodies piling up and family dysfunction with a secret from Evelyns past coming back to haunt her. Will is unable to commit and talk about low self esteem and abandonment issues. <br /><br />The reveal at the end of her illegitimate son from a Mexican lover who Evelyn put into a loving family makes no sense to me. Why kidnap her when he did not want the money? Get himself trapped? <br /><br />The son Caleb goes off the rails and wants vengeance for being in his mind abandoned. Luckily he is a talker and in the critical scene Evelyn, even though tortured and severely injured saves her daughter. I found the motive implausible but did enjoy the story and plan to read the next one, Criminal where Will’s father is paroled from prison. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_392965138" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/392965138" />
    <a title="Elise Moto" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9294238-elise-moto"><img alt="Elise Moto" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/392965138?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise Moto" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise Moto" href="/user/show/9294238-elise-moto">Elise Moto</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392965138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13898899508268248486">To tell the truth, with this one I found myself yawning over the detailed forensics and skipping all of it to get to what is most interesting, which is Will and Sara's relationship. I found myself losing interest in the main plot, which was the disappearance of Faith's mother. I think my thing is characters, not forensics and procedures. As mentioned regarding other books in this series, Slaughter has done an about-turn with Angie, suddenly portraying her as a 'bee-atch' who delights in pushing </span>
  <span id="freeText13898899508268248486" style="display:none">To tell the truth, with this one I found myself yawning over the detailed forensics and skipping all of it to get to what is most interesting, which is Will and Sara's relationship. I found myself losing interest in the main plot, which was the disappearance of Faith's mother. I think my thing is characters, not forensics and procedures. As mentioned regarding other books in this series, Slaughter has done an about-turn with Angie, suddenly portraying her as a 'bee-atch' who delights in pushing Will's pain buttons and ridiculing him. I don't like this sudden one-dimensional portrayal of a character who was multi-layered and sympathetic in book 1 (Triptych, which by now is the best book in the series). This is what happens with series. You can't please all of your readers, and I'm starting to get disenchanted with this one. But I still love to see Will throw off his chains (that would be Angie) and embrace a new love, and allow himself to be treated with respect. In a way, Sara is not only his lover but the good parent he never had. He seems like such a nice guy. Plus, as Sara noted, he has the most gorgeous legs she's ever seen on a man.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13898899508268248486" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
